## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring forces), velocity v (damping forces), and possibly time t (external driving). The nonlinearity can appear in any of these dependencies.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring force plus linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (linear with harmonic driving)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with driving)
- Quintic restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear potential)
- Quadratic-cubic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Driven van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (driven self-excited oscillator)
- Coulomb-damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (v**2)**(-0.5) (sign-dependent friction approximation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Position-velocity coupling terms like x**2 * v → amplitude-dependent damping (van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal time dependence cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) → external periodic driving force
- Cubic position term x**3 with same/opposite sign as linear term → hardening/softening spring nonlinearity
- Odd powers of velocity (v, v**3) → dissipative forces preserving time-reversal antisymmetry
- Even powers of x multiplying v (x**2 * v) → self-excitation or limit cycle behavior
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system (conservative or dissipative)
- Mixed polynomial in x with even and odd powers → asymmetric potential (broken symmetry)

GT Equivalence Verification (PO26)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*x**c3
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.826056547542989*v - 2.45151654379511*x**3 - 0.413028273771494*log(Abs(v) + 1) + 0.340325443007139*sin(t)`

The key terms are:
1. Linear in v: `-0.826*v`
2. Cubic in x: `-2.45*x**3`
3. Logarithmic in |v|: `-0.413*log(|v| + 1)`
4. Sinusoidal in t: `0.34*sin(t)`

The critical challenge is the `log(|v| + 1)` term. None of the candidates contain a logarithm explicitly. So the question is: can any combination of terms in the candidates approximate or exactly equal `log(|v| + 1)`?

Let me think about this carefully. The `log(|v| + 1)` term is a specific nonlinear function of v that involves an absolute value. No polynomial in v (like v², v³, v*x², etc.) can be equivalent to `log(|v| + 1)` for all values of v. Similarly, `exp(...)` terms in t won't help with this.

Let me also consider: could `cos(c4*sin(c5*t + c6))` somehow help? No, this is a function of t only, not v.

Could `exp(c*x²)` or similar terms help? No, these are functions of x, not v.

Could `v*|v|` (in candidate 2) equal `log(|v|+1)`? No, `v*|v| = |v|*v` which is v² for v>0 and -v² for v<0. This is not log(|v|+1).

Could `x*cos(c*x)` help? No, this is a function of x.

Could `x/(c*x² + 1)` help? No, function of x only.

None of the candidates contain:
- `log(...)` 
- `Abs(v)` (except candidate 2 which has `v*Abs(v)`)

The term `-0.413*log(|v|+1)` is an essential part of the GT that cannot be reproduced by any polynomial, trigonometric, or exponential combination of terms available in the candidates.

Let me double-check candidate 2: `c0*x + c1*x**2 + c2*x**3 + c3*v + c4 + c5*exp(c6*sin(c7*t + c8)) + c9*v*Abs(v)`

This has `v*|v|` which is a nonlinear function of v, but it equals `v²*sign(v)`, which is not `log(|v|+1)`.

For the `exp(c6*sin(...))` terms: if c6 is very small, we can Taylor expand `exp(c6*sin(θ)) ≈ 1 + c6*sin(θ)`, giving a constant plus a sinusoidal term. This could match the constant + sin(t) part. But this still doesn't give us `log(|v|+1)`.

No candidate contains a logarithmic term or any mechanism to produce `log(|v|+1)`. Since this is a function that varies with v and is fundamentally different from any polynomial, exponential, or trigonometric function, no candidate can match the GT exactly.

Let me verify there isn't some clever algebraic identity I'm missing. The GT has `log(|v|+1)` which:
- Is even in v (symmetric)
- Grows logarithmically
- Has a specific curvature

No finite polynomial in v can equal this. No `exp(...)` of v terms appear in the candidates. The only non-polynomial v terms are `v*|v|` in candidate 2, which doesn't help.

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.826056547542989*v - 2.45151654379511*x**3 - 0.413028273771494*log(Abs(v) + 1) + 0.340325443007139*sin(t)`

The GT contains these basis functions:
1. `v` (linear in v)
2. `x**3` (cubic in x)
3. `log(Abs(v) + 1)` (logarithmic in |v|)
4. `sin(t)` (sinusoidal in t)

The key challenge is the `log(Abs(v) + 1)` term. No polynomial, exponential, or trigonometric combination of `v` can exactly reproduce a logarithmic function. This is because `log(|v| + 1)` is a fundamentally different basis function.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of a `log` term or something that could produce one:

**None of the candidates contain a `log` function.** They all use combinations of polynomials in x and v, trigonometric functions of t, exponentials, and rational functions.

The candidates try to approximate `log(Abs(v) + 1)` using:
- `v**3` terms (Candidates 1, 4, 5, 9, 13, 14, etc.)
- `v*x**2` terms (Candidates 1, 3, 6, 7, etc.)
- `v*Abs(v)` terms (Candidate 2)
- `exp(...)` terms (Candidates 2, 3, 4, 8, etc.)
- Various other polynomial terms

**Critical analysis:** The term `log(Abs(v) + 1)` is NOT a polynomial in v, NOT an exponential, NOT a trigonometric function, and NOT a rational function. By the principle of linear independence of basis functions:

- No finite polynomial in v can equal `log(|v| + 1)` for all v
- No exponential function can equal `log(|v| + 1)` for all v  
- `v*Abs(v)` is not equal to `log(|v| + 1)` for all v
- `cos(c*sin(...))` is not a log function
- Rational functions like `x/(x²+1)` don't help with the v-dependence

Since every candidate lacks a `log(Abs(v) + 1)` term (or any logarithmic term in v), and this term cannot be reproduced by any combination of the basis functions present in the candidates, **none of the candidates can exactly match the GT**.

Let me verify there's no clever cancellation possible: The GT has a non-trivial dependence on `v` through `log(|v|+1)`. This function has a specific curvature profile that differs from any polynomial or other elementary function. No setting of constants can make polynomials, exponentials, or trig functions equal to a logarithm over the entire domain.
